        <hr> 
        <h1 id="payments-overview">Payments API</h1> 
        <p> Our payments API lets you accept bitcoin without worrying about the inner workings of the bitcoin Price and the bitcoin Network. </p> 
        <p> You just tell us the amount to charge in the customer's currency and we'll quote the bitcoin equivalent and set up a unique Bitcoin Address for the bitcoin to be sent to. Each payment corresponds to a different bitcoin address. </p> 
        <p> You can send bitcoin addresses via email, show them in your checkout using your own UI libraries, or easier yet: You can <a href="#setup-pos">setup your own Bitex powered point of sale</a> and use the user friendly <a href="#payment-page">Payment's Page.</a> </p> 
        <p> All Bitcoins received as payment will be sold automatically at the best BTC/USD market price in Bitex. You can optionally decide to keep part of the received Bitcoin and withdraw or sell them at a later date. </p> 
        <p> Both USD and/or BTC received as payment will be credited to your Bitex Balance and can be withdrawn as per our supported cash-out methods. </p> 
        <p class="text-danger"> Payments which are too small for our orderbook (roughly 2 USD or less) will not be settled automatically. They will be kept as bitcoin in your balance and it's up to you to decide when to sell them. </p> 
        <p> Contact us if you need settlements in currencies other than BTC or USD; if you need to have a guaranteed price instead of settling at the best BTC/USD price; or if you need to automatically settle lots of micro-payments. </p> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_create_a_payment"> 
         <h2> <strong>Create a Payment</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Send us an amount and currency, and we'll quote it in bitcoin and give you an address where the payment is expected. The bitcoins will credit to your Bitex account and can be sold automatically to get the original amount in your requested currency. </p> 
          <p> Payments have an expiration of 1 hour, the bitcoin transaction must be initiated within that timeframe, if your customer takes longer you can always create a new payment and get a new quote and bitcoin address. If someone pays to an address after the payment is expired the bitcoin quantity will still be credited to your bitex.la, so it's possible for you to issue a refund and/or forward the received bitcoin to a new payment address yourself. </p> 
          <p> You can provide a callback_url to get notifications about a payment, read more in the Payment Callbacks section. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">POST</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>private/payments</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your Bitex.la API key.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"currency_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Currency in which the amount to be quoted is expresse, possible values are:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"amount"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1000</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Amount to be quoted, in currency. If currency_id is 1 (BTC) then no quotation will be made and this exact bitcoin amount will be expected as payment</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"callback_url"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"https://example.com/ipn"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. We'll POST your full payment as JSON to this URL everytime its status changes. Your callback_url must be https</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"keep"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">25</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. Percentage of the received bitcoin to keep as such, instead of converting it to Fiat</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// when payment is settled. This is ignored when you quote your payment in Bitcoin (passing currency_id=1),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// as it's assumed you're keeping 100% of the bitcoin received as bitcoin.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"customer_reference"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"An Alto latte, no sugar"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. Reason for this payment, as understood by the payer.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_reference"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"invoice#1234"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. Reason for this payment, as understood by you, payee.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Bitex id for this payment.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"user_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// This is you.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"amount"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">100.00</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Amount that was quoted to its BTC equivalent</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"currency_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Currency you requested to quote to BTC., This is not the settlement currency,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// You could quote the equivalent of 100 UYU in BTC, but when payment clears</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// we'll sell the received bitcoin for USD, not UYU, and credit USD to your balance.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Possible values are:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 1 - Bitcoin (BTC, No need to quote)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 3 - United States Dollar (USD)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 4 - Argentine Peso (ARS)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 5 - Uruguayan Peso (UYU)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 6 - Euro (EUR)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 7 - Chilean Peso (CLP)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 8 - Peruvian New Sol (PEN)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 9 - Brazilian Real (BRL)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 10 - Colombian Peso (COP)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 11 - Mexican Peso (MXN)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"expected_quantity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.02</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Quoted amount in BTC. Payment will be considered done if at least this much bitcoin credits in the provided address</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"previous_expected_quantity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.018</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Previous expected quantity, before this payment's quote was updated. Starts as null. Payment will be considered done if at least this much bitcoin credits in the provided address</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"confirmed_quantity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Bitcoin quantity received (so far)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"unconfirmed_quantity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Next Bitcoin quantity, after funds in transit have credited.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"valid_until"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1430226201</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Payment expiration date as a unix epoch. The confirmed_quantity must be equal (or greater than)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// the expected_quantity before the valid_until date, otherwise the payment is expired.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Unfulfilled payments expire after an hour of being created.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"quote_valid_until"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1430226201</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Unix epoch when the quote_valid_until time is reached,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// the payment will be re-quoted, changing the expected_quantity.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The previous_expected_quantity is kept around, and is still a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// valid expected quantity for payment processing purposes until</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// the next expiration. When currency_id is 1 (BTC) quote_valid_until</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// is the same as the valid_until, as the payment is never re-quoted</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"last_quoted_on"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1430220201</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Unix epoch for the time this payment was last quoted. Starts out as the payment creation time</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"status"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"pending"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// This payment's status, one of:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "pending" - Just created.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "seen" - The expected_quantity is in transit.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "done" - The expected_quantity was received.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "settled" - Funds were credited to your balance</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "expired" - Payment was not seen before expiration date.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "cancelled" - Payment was seen but didn't confirm for 2 hours, due to unknown or unexpected circumstances.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Bitcoin address where payment is expected.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"address"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"public_address"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"1ABC..."</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"payment_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"auto_sell"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">false</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">},</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"settlement_currency_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// A payment may be settled to a currency different than the quoted one.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Most payments will be settled to USD at the current Bitex market price,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// or left as BTC. Select Bitex clients may have their payments settled to another currency of their choice.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 1 - Bitcoin (BTC)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 3 - United States Dollar (USD)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"settlement_amount: null, // The amount of settlement_currency credited to your corresponding balance for this payment when settled keep"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">1.5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// You can choose to keep a percentage of the bitcoin received and only settle the rest.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// This has no effect if you quoted BTC as we assume you were intending on keeping 100% of it as settlement</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"kept"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.0003</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The Bitcoin quantity that was not settled to Fiat and kept as bitcoin instead, as configured in the keep field.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// You may also end up keeping bitcoin if the amount to settle is less than 2 USD or if any other unexpected situation is encountered at settlement time.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"overpaid"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// If a customer accidentally pays more than expected the amount will be registered here.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// If that happens they will probably contact you for a refund, which you can issue by requesting a bitcoin withdrawal to a bitcoin address they provide.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_reference"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. Reason for this payment as understood by you, the merchant. This is not modifiable by the customer</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"customer_reference"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. Reason for this payment as understood by the customer.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="9">curl -X POST https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/private/payments -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_api_key",
  "currency_id": 3,
  "amount": 1000,
  "callback_url": "https://example.com/ipn",
  "keep": 25,
  "customer_reference": "An Alto latte, no sugar",
  "merchant_reference": "invoice#1234"
}'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_show_a_payment"> 
         <h2> <strong>Show a Payment</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> If you rather use a Pull model instead of callbacks, or if you think you've missed something, you can always query your payment information like this. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">GET</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>private/payments/<strong>payment_id</strong></em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your bitex.la API key</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Bitex id for this payment.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"user_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// This is you.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"amount"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">100.00</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Amount that was quoted to its BTC equivalent</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"currency_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Currency you requested to quote to BTC., This is not the settlement currency,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// You could quote the equivalent of 100 UYU in BTC, but when payment clears</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// we'll sell the received bitcoin for USD, not UYU, and credit USD to your balance.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Possible values are:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 1 - Bitcoin (BTC, No need to quote)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 3 - United States Dollar (USD)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 4 - Argentine Peso (ARS)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 5 - Uruguayan Peso (UYU)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 6 - Euro (EUR)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 7 - Chilean Peso (CLP)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 8 - Peruvian New Sol (PEN)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 9 - Brazilian Real (BRL)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 10 - Colombian Peso (COP)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 11 - Mexican Peso (MXN)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"expected_quantity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.02</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Quoted amount in BTC. Payment will be considered done if at least this much bitcoin credits in the provided address</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"previous_expected_quantity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.018</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Previous expected quantity, before this payment's quote was updated. Starts as null. Payment will be considered done if at least this much bitcoin credits in the provided address</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"confirmed_quantity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Bitcoin quantity received (so far)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"unconfirmed_quantity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Next Bitcoin quantity, after funds in transit have credited.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"valid_until"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1430226201</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Payment expiration date as a unix epoch. The confirmed_quantity must be equal (or greater than)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// the expected_quantity before the valid_until date, otherwise the payment is expired.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Unfulfilled payments expire after an hour of being created.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"quote_valid_until"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1430226201</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Unix epoch when the quote_valid_until time is reached,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// the payment will be re-quoted, changing the expected_quantity.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The previous_expected_quantity is kept around, and is still a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// valid expected quantity for payment processing purposes until</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// the next expiration. When currency_id is 1 (BTC) quote_valid_until</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// is the same as the valid_until, as the payment is never re-quoted</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"last_quoted_on"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1430220201</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Unix epoch for the time this payment was last quoted. Starts out as the payment creation time</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"status"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"pending"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// This payment's status, one of:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "pending" - Just created.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "seen" - The expected_quantity is in transit.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "done" - The expected_quantity was received.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "settled" - Funds were credited to your balance</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "expired" - Payment was not seen before expiration date.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// "cancelled" - Payment was seen but didn't confirm for 2 hours, due to unknown or unexpected circumstances.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Bitcoin address where payment is expected.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"address"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"public_address"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"1ABC..."</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"payment_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"auto_sell"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">false</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">},</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"settlement_currency_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// A payment may be settled to a currency different than the quoted one.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Most payments will be settled to USD at the current Bitex market price,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// or left as BTC. Select Bitex clients may have their payments settled to another currency of their choice.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 1 - Bitcoin (BTC)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// 3 - United States Dollar (USD)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"settlement_amount"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The amount of settlement_currency credited to your corresponding balance for this payment when settled</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"keep"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">1.5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// You can choose to keep a percentage of the bitcoin received and only settle the rest.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// This has no effect if you quoted BTC as we assume you were intending on keeping 100% of it as settlement</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"kept"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.0003</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The Bitcoin quantity that was not settled to Fiat and kept as bitcoin instead, as configured in the keep field.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// You may also end up keeping bitcoin if the amount to settle is less than 2 USD or if any other unexpected situation is encountered at settlement time.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"overpaid"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">0.0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// If a customer accidentally pays more than expected the amount will be registered here.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// If that happens they will probably contact you for a refund, which you can issue by requesting a bitcoin withdrawal to a bitcoin address they provide.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_reference"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. Reason for this payment as understood by you, the merchant. This is not modifiable by the customer</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"customer_reference"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. Reason for this payment as understood by the customer.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="3">curl -X GET https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/private/payments/&lt;payment_id&gt; -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_api_key"
}'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_list_all_payment"> 
         <h2> <strong>List all Payment</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> List all your latest payments, newest first. You can optionally filter by status. Results may be truncated after 500 rows. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">GET</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>private/payments</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your Bitex.la API key.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"status"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"done"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Optional. You can filter payments by status.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div>

        <div class="docs-box" id="payment-callbacks"> 
         <h2>Payment Callbacks</h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> When a callback_url is set for a payment Bitex will POST updates to it everytime a payment status changes. </p> 
          <p> Your callback_url must be HTTPS because we want to make sure we're only contacting you, and it will include your first active API key in it, so that you know it's us sending the callback. Your API key is our shared secret, so you may want to handle it the same way you handle your users login credentials, hiding it from web server request logs for example. </p> 
          <p> Our request's content type will be <strong>application/json</strong> and the content will be a structure containing your API key and the payment is it would be returned when querying its status. </p> 
          <p> Here's a <strong>curl</strong> invokation that mimics a Bitex callback, you can copy and paste it directly into your terminal. </p> 
          <div class="well well-sm">
            curl -s -H 'Content-Type: application/json' -d \ '{ "api_key": "your_api_key", "payment": { "id":1, "user_id":1, "amount":100.0, "currency_id": 1, "expected_quantity":0.01936, "previous_expected_quantity":0.019, "confirmed_quantity":0.0, "unconfirmed_quantity":0.0, "status":"pending", "address": { "id":11012, "public_address":"mgj8dsnp48iGA8WNfk4y2PHj8HcugvxUj2" }, "valid_until": 1430230348, "quote_valid_until": 1430230348, "last_quoted_on": 1430210000, "settlement_amount": null, "settlement_currency_id": null, "keep": 0.0, "customer_reference": null, "merchant_reference": null, } }' \ 'https://your_url/callback_handler' 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <hr> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="pos-overview"> 
         <h2>Web Point of Sale</h2> 
         <p> We have a Web Point of Sale you can use to display your payment's information to customers. </p> 
         <p> Your point of sale conveniently displays any payment address and amount as a QR code that can be scanned with a standard bitcoin wallet. It can even be embedded in your e-commerce checkout page and report back on the payment status for a seamless integration. </p> 
         <p> The point of sale can also be used for self-service payment request from your customers, where they can specify how much they want to pay and the payment reason. </p> 
         <p> You need to configure your Web Point of Sale before you can start using it, please reffer to <a href="#setup-pos">Setup Web POS.</a> </p> 
        </div> 
        <br> 
        <br> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="payment-page"> 
         <h2>Payment Page</h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Your virtual Point of Sale can display all your payment information for your customers to conveniently pay using their Bitcoin wallet. </p> 
          <p> Payment pages can be loaded stand alone or within an iframe inside your own checkout flow, using the <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/Window/postMessage"> postMessage Web API </a> to report the <a href="#show-payment">full JSON payment</a> to the parent window. </p> 
          <p> Check out <a href="https://jsfiddle.net/nubis/wo5v59yn" target="_blank"> this example in jsfiddle.net </a> using jQuery and Twitter Bootstrap to show a Payment Page in a modal iframe and closing it a few seconds after the payment is recognized as paid. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span>GET</span> 
           <span class="url"> https://bitex.la/pos/ <em> <strong>merchant_slug</strong> / <strong>payment_bitcoin_address</strong> </em> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>Screenshots</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <div class="row screenshots"> 
            <div class="col-xs-6"> 
             <img class="img-responsive" src="/images/payment-pending.png" alt="Payment pending"> 
            </div> 
            <div class="col-xs-6"> 
             <img class="img-responsive" src="/images/payment-done.png" alt="Payment done"> 
            </div> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="self-service-pos"> 
         <h2>Self Service POS</h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> By configuring your web POS you get a user friendly page where either you or your customers can create new payments at will. </p> 
          <p> They just need to specify an amount and currency to quote, and a reference for the payment so you know where it's from. The amount and reference can be pre-configured in the URL. </p> 
          <p> Your Self Service POS is the most frictionless way to start accepting payments with bitex. </p> 
          <p> You can also accept donations via the self service pos, we have a special URL that shows the standard POS but calls the payment a 'Donation' which is friendlier for your donors. This is just cosmetic, there's no internal distinction between payments and donations in your bitex payments dashboard. </p> 
         </div> 
         <strong>Standard URL</strong> 
         <div class="well well-sm"> 
          <span class="method">GET</span> 
          <span class="url"> https://bitex.la/ <em>pos/</em> <strong>merchant_slug</strong> </span> 
         </div> 
         <strong>Screenshots</strong> 
         <div class="well well-sm"> 
          <div class="row"> 
           <div class="col-md-12"> 
            <img class="img-responsive" src="/images/self-service-empty.png" alt="Self service empty"> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <strong>URL with prepopulated fields</strong> 
         <div class="well well-sm"> 
          <span class="method">GET</span> 
          <span class="url"> https://bitex.la/ <em>pos/</em> <strong>merchant_slug</strong> ?amount=150&amp;currency_id=4&amp;customer_reference=Fruit Basket </span> 
         </div> 
         <strong>Screenshots with prepopulated fields</strong> 
         <div class="well well-sm"> 
          <div class="row"> 
           <div class="col-md-12"> 
            <img class="img-responsive" src="/images/self-service-filled.png" alt="Self service filled"> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <strong>Donations URL</strong> 
         <div class="well well-sm"> 
          <span class="method">GET</span> 
          <span class="url"> https://bitex.la/ <em>donate/</em> <strong>merchant_slug</strong> </span> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_setup_web_pos"> 
         <h2> <strong>Setup Web POS</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Configures your Web POS in a url of your choice. You should set all fields for the first time so that your POS is enabled. </p> 
          <p> After the initial setup you can change each field independently by only posting the field you wish to change. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">POST</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>private/payments/pos_setup</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your Bitex.la API key.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_name"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Tierra Buena"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your business name</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_slug"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"tierrabuena"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Last part of your POS URL. Lowercase letters, numbers and dashes only.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Must not be taken by someone else.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// You can check if it already exists visiting https://bitex.la/pos/your_desired_name</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_logo"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"https://t.co/logo.png"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Public URL of your logo.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// We reccommend your logo to be at least 200px in height and no more than 300px in width.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// It should look good in a Bitex blue background. Also, try to keep the file-size as small</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// as possible otherwise it may slow down your POS loading time.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_keep"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The bitcoin percentage to keep instead of settling to USD for payments created in the self service POS.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Defaults to 0, which means you won't keep any bitcoin.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_site"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"https://example.com"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your website URL. A link to it will be shown in your self service point of sale</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_name"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Tierra Buena"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your business name</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_slug"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"tierrabuena"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Last part of your POS URL.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_logo"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"https://t.co/logo.png"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Public URL of your logo.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_keep"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// How much bitcoin to keep for Payments created via Web POS</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"merchant_site"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"https://example.com"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your website URL.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="8">curl -X POST https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/private/payments/pos_setup -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_api_key",
  "merchant_name": "Tierra Buena",
  "merchant_slug": "tierrabuena",
  "merchant_logo": "https://t.co/logo.png",
  "merchant_keep": 0,
  "merchant_site": "https://example.com"
}'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <hr> 
        <h1 id="resellers">Resellers</h1> 
        <p> Bitex resellers can create and manage Bitex Users (accounts) through specially issued API Keys. If you need to manage several Bitex accounts please contact us at <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#432b262f2f2c03212a37263b6d2f22"><span class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="c2aaa7aeaead82a0abb6a7baecaea3">[email&nbsp;protected]</span></a> to get a reseller API key. </p> 
        <p> A reseller API key has all permissions to do anything on a given user's behalf. All API endpoints remain the same, but a new <strong>as_user</strong> parameter is introduced to specify which of the reseller's users is being impersonated. </p> 
        <p> Users created by a reseller act the same as regular users that signup through the website. They need to provide a full KYC, they have their own balances, and if they know their email and password they can even log-in to the website. </p> 
        <p> If you don't want your users to log-in and want to use their accounts through API you can just craete them with a random password that you don't store anywhere. </p> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_create_user"> 
         <h2> <strong>Create User</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Registers a new user for your reseller, returning the newly created user_id and kyc_profile_id. </p> 
          <p> Your next step should be <a href="#impersonating">impersonating</a> this user to complete their KYC Profile. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">POST</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>/reseller/users</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your Bitex.la API key.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"email"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"<a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection" class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="8fe5e0e7e1cfeaf7eee2ffe3eaa1ece0e2">[email&nbsp;protected]</a>"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The customer email. They may receive email notifications to this address.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// If you'd rather receive the emails yourself you can sign them up with a tagged address like <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection" class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="fc859389d796939492bc8593898e9893919d9592d29f9391">[email&nbsp;protected]</a></span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"password"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"5up3r53cr37"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Their password to log-in through the Bitex website.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// You can set it to some random long string if you don't plan to log-in as this user.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"user_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">5000</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The newly created user ID.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"kyc_profile_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">5010</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The user's default KYC Profile id. Your next step should be impersonating this user to complete their KYC Profile.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="5">curl -X POST https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest//reseller/users -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_api_key",
  "email": "john@example.com",
  "password": "5up3r53cr37"
}'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_list_your_users"> 
         <h2> <strong>List your users</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> List all users associated to this reseller. Can be retrieved both as JSON or CSV. </p> 
          <p> Your next step should be <a href="#impersonatin">impersonating</a> this user to complete their KYC Profile. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">GET</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>reseller/users</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your bitex.la API key</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">[</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// User ID.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"<a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection" class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="80eaefe8eec0e5f8e1edf0ece5aee3efed">[email&nbsp;protected]</a>"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// User email.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">10000.00000000</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Total USD.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">500.00000000</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Available USD.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">20.00000000</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Total BTC.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mf">1.00000000</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Available BTC.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"1aBcdeF..."</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Default BTC deposit address.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="3">curl -X GET https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/reseller/users -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_api_key"
}'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_impersonating_users"> 
         <h2> <strong>Impersonating Users</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Resellers can impersonate their users for regular API endpoints using their special reseller API key and including an <strong>as_user</strong> parameter with the ID of the user to impersonate. </p> 
          <p> See <a href="#impersonating-example">this example</a> updating a KYC Profile for a user as a Reseller. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">POST</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>private...</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your Bitex.la API key.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"as_user"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">5000</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// User ID to impersonate in this call</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"..."</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"..."</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Extra parameters for the API endpoint.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="5">curl -X POST https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/private... -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_api_key",
  "as_user": 5000,
  "...": "..."
}'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_example_impersonating_to_update_kyc"> 
         <h2> <strong>Example: Impersonating to update KYC</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> This is an example of how to impersonate one of your users to complete their KYC Profile. </p> 
          <p> All changes will be reviewed by a compliance officer, as with any other request to update a KYC Profile. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">GET</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>reseller/users</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your Bitex.la API key.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"as_user"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">5000</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// User ID to impersonate in this call</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"usage_tier"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"micro"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Usage tier you want to get into one of" micro, small, medium or large.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"first_name"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Billy"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"last_name"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Bob"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"personal_id_number"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"33222111N"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// No particular format expected, just make sure it's a valid id number.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"personal_id_issuer_country"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"AR"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Uppercase ISO country code for the country that issued the ID</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"personal_id_type"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"passport"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Type of ID provided. It's free form but we suggest values like 'dni', 'passport', 'drivers_license'</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"tax_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4333222115</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// This persons tax id (cuit for argentina)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"birth_date"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"1970/1/30"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Year/Month/Date</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"nationality"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"brazilian"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"gender"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"male"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// We suggest male or female</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"occupation"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Singer"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"home_address"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Argentina, Bue..."</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Full address, including zipcode</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"work_address"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Argentina, Bue..."</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Full address, including zipcode</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"phone_numbers"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"555120921"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"legal_entity"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Boolean: Wheter they will be # operating on behalf of a company # or other legal entity.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"politically_exposed_person"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Boolean: Wheter they are what's # considered to be politically exposed.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">[</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">12345678</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Kyc Profile id.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Billy"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Name</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Bob"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Last Name.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"33222111N"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Personal ID Number</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"AR"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// ISO country code for the issuer of this ID.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"passport"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Type of ID</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"4332221115"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Tax Id</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">946685400</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Birth date as unix timestamp.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"brazilian"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Nationality</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"male"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Gender</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Singer"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Occupation</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Argentina, Bue..."</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Home address.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"Argentina, Bue..."</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Work address.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"+51 555 120921"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Phone</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Is legal entity.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Is politically exposed.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"micro"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Requested usage tier.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"micro"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Current usage tier as accepted by our compliance officers.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="20">curl -X GET https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/reseller/users -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_api_key",
  "as_user": 5000,
  "usage_tier": "micro",
  "first_name": "Billy",
  "last_name": "Bob",
  "personal_id_number": "33222111N",

        <hr> 
        <h1 id="concierge">Concierge</h1> 
        <p> Our Concierge service let's you issue one-to-many payments in local currency, using a network of partners built by Bitex.la. <a href="https://blog.bitex.la/how-does-concierge-works/">Learn more here.</a> </p> 
        <p> The concierge service focuses on lowering costs and offering transparency. Therefore, each Work Order Request is quoted independently and all the fees involved are shared with you in full detail. </p> 
        <h3>How to use the Concierge service?</h3> 
        <ol> 
         <li> Become a reseller <br> Contact us so that we give you a Reseller API. Also, read up on our Reseller API usage <a href="#resellers">here</a> </li> 
         <li> Create your Users <br> Both the Payer and the Payees must belong to your Reseller. <a href="#create-user">Learn more here.</a> </li> 
         <li> Create Withdrawal Instructions <br> At least one for each one of your payees too. <a href="#create-withdrawal-instruction">Learn more here.</a> </li> 
         <li> Create your Work Order Request. <br> You'll specify <strong>inputs</strong> (the money you send to concierge) and <strong>outputs</strong> (the money concierge should send to each payee). </li> 
         <li> Wait for us to acknowledge <br> After that, keep refreshing your Work Order Request to see if we've accepted it (we usually will). <br> If it's accepted one of our account officers may contact you to quote how much money you need to use to fund your "inputs" and give you the bank instructions. This information may also be available for each 'input' in the data returned by the API. 
          <div class="text-warning">
            The Concierge process may end up being cheaper than quoted, if so, you'll get a rebate in your Bitex.la balance. 
          </div> </li> 
         <li> Optionally, wait for a better price. <br> Since our prices fluctuate constantly, the quoted amounts in your inputs or outputs may change from the time you send funds to your inputs to the time we receive them and are ready to start the process on our end. We can call you and give you a chance to delay the process waiting for a more favorable price. You'll probably want to do this confirmation step for your first Work Order Requests, but may want to skip it once you become familiar with the Concierge service and pricing. </li> 
         <li> Finally, wait while we do our magic. <br> Periodically refresh your Work Order Request. Look at the outputs as all the payees get paid, until the status becomes 'done'. If any problems should arise an account officer will contact you or the payee, depending on your preference. 
          <div class="text-warning">
           Concierge will do everything it can to get the money to each payee.
          </div> </li> 
        </ol> 
        <p> When sending money using concierge, you may fall into one of the following two use cases. The way you construct your inputs and outputs will determine which one. Exactly one input or one output amount should be left empty to note who's bearing the cost for this transaction. </p> 
        <h3>You need to pay a number of people, bearing all the costs yourself.</h3> 
        <p> For this, you'll leave one of your input amounts empty. We'll calculate the cost for sending the money to all the payees and quote how much to need to send for that. </p> 
        <h3> You have a fixed amount to spend, one of the payees will bear the cost of the transaction. </h3> 
        <p> For this, you'll leave one of your output amounts empty. We'll ensure all your payees get the specified amount, and send the rest to the remaining one. This kind of transfer is trickier to calculate as you may not want one payee to bear the cost for all the others, you may want to instruct less money to go to each payee to lighten the burden on the payee whose amount you leave empty. Future versions of this API will allow you to more fairly distribute the costs between payees. </p> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_create_work_order_request"> 
         <h2> <strong>Create Work Order Request</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Creates a new work order request to receive one payment from you (inputs) and issue several payments to a number of payees (outputs). </p> 
          <p> Responses use the <strong>json:api</strong> format, learn more at <a href="http://jsonapi.org">http://jsonapi.org/</a> </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">POST</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>reseller/work_order_requests</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_reseller_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"payer_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">123</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The payer must belong to your reseller.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Once inputs credit, we can call you and confirm how much will be spent from each input,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// and how much will be received by each payee. the outputs could be considered as the</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// cost of the international clearing network.</span><span class="w"> </span><span the concierge network partner when receiving</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// money from the bitcoin clearing network.</span><span class="w"> </span><span </span><span class="c1">// Cash_out fees are taken by the payee's bank and our partner's bank.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// These fees are percentual and/or fixed, and start out as null.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"cash_out_fee_percent"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">null</span><span class="p">,</span><span         <div class="docs-box" id="api_show_work_order_request"> 
         <h2> <strong>Show Work Order Request</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Show a work order request in JSON API format. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">GET</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>reseller/work_order_requests/<strong>work_order_request</strong></em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your bitex.la API key</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"data"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"1"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The work order request ID.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"type"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"work_order_requests"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"attributes"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"payer_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The status will change as your order progresses</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// received: We received your request and are doing sanity checks on it.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// waiting_for_inputs: We're contacting you to give you instructions to fund your inputs.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// sending_to_outputs: We're in the process of issuing all payments to payees.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// done: This Work Order Request has been completed, nothing else to do here.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// cancelled: Orders can be cancelled, usually before you fund your inputs.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"status"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"received"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Our pricing fluctuates slightly throughout the day. Input and output amounts</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// may change between the time que request funding for your inputs and the time</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// those funds credit and we can move forward issuing the payouts.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// We can call you once all your inputs are funded so you can decide to move</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// forward, or wait until the price changes in your favor.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"should_confirm_quote"</span><span Bitcoin.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// We can configure your Bitex account so that these bitcoin are converted</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// to USD upon arrival just contact us to make that change.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"bitcoin_rebate"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Last time your request saw any updates.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"updated_at"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"2000-01-01T00:00:00.000Z"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">},</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// As per the JSON API specification, relatioships are defined as references</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// When parsing, you may want to look at "included" for each input and output.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"relationships"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"inputs"</span><span class="p">:</span><span         <div class="docs-box" id="api_list_work_order_requests"> 
         <h2> <strong>List Work Order Requests</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Show a work order requests list in JSON API format. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">GET</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>reseller/work_order_requests</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your bitex.la API key</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"data"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"1"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The work order request ID.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"type"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"work_order_requests"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"attributes"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"payer_id"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The status will change as your order progresses</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// received: We received your request and are doing sanity checks on it.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// waiting_for_inputs: We're contacting you to give you instructions to fund your inputs.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// sending_to_outputs: We're in the process of issuing all payments to payees.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// done: This Work Order Request has been completed, nothing else to do here.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// cancelled: Orders can be cancelled, usually before you fund your inputs.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"status"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"received"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Our pricing fluctuates slightly throughout the day. class="c1">// those funds credit and we can move forward issuing the payouts.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// We can call you once all your inputs are funded so you can decide to         <hr> 
        <h1 id="webhooks">Webhooks</h1> 
        <p> Resellers can configure a single webhook URL to receive updates about their changing entities. </p> 
        <p> Updates will be sent via a POST request to your URL. The body of the request will contain the full entity in json-api format. </p> 
        <p> The request will contain a 'Webhook-Auth' header, with a SHA256 hexdigest of your first API key, so you can authenticate the callback originates on our end. You can calculate your API key's SHA256 in *nix like so: </p>
        <pre>'$ echo -n your_api_key | sha256sum'</pre> Alternatively, you can use the 
        <a href="#test-webhook-url">Test Webhook endpoint</a> and check the 'Webhook-Auth' being posted to your URL. 
        <p></p> 
        <h3>WorkOrderRequest callbacks</h3> 
        <p> WorkOrderRequests trigger callbacks whenever they are created and as they move through the flow until being <strong>done</strong> </p> 
        <h3>KycProfile callbacks</h3> 
        <p> KycProfiles trigger callbacks whenever they are accepted or rejected by one of our admins. You can check the 'data.attributes.accepted_usage_tier' field in in the callback body to know if a user was accepted or rejected. It's null when it was rejected, and a string describing the usage tier when it's accepted. Notice a KycProfile may change from accepted to rejected at any time, it may be accepted when first created then get rejected by further compliance procedures. </p> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_show_webhook_url"> 
         <h2> <strong>Show Webhook URL</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Show a work order requests list in JSON API format. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">GET</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>reseller/webhook</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_api_key"</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Your bitex.la API key</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="nt">"webhook_url"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"https://example.com/webhook"</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="3">curl -X GET https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/reseller/webhook -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_api_key"
}'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_update_webhook_url"> 
         <h2> <strong>Update Webhook URL</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Setup a webhook URL to receive callbacks. The URL must be https </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">PUT</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>/reseller/webhook</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_reseller_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"webhook_url"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"https://example.com/webhook"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Any HTTPS url.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="nt">"webhook_url"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"https://example.com/webhook"</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>cURL example pastebox</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="4">curl -X PUT https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest//reseller/webhook -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
  "api_key": "your_reseller_api_key",
  "webhook_url": "https://example.com/webhook"
}'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="docs-box" id="api_test_webhook_url"> 
         <h2> <strong>Test Webhook URL</strong> </h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Test your URL, this will trigger a callback with a simple JSON body, echoing your params. </p> 
          <strong>URL</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span class="method">POST</span> 
           <span class="url">https://bitex.la/api-v1/rest/<em>reseller/webhook/test</em></span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Request</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"api_key"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"your_reseller_api_key"</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nt">"echo"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"hello world"</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// Any message you want echoed.</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span> 
          </div> 
          <strong>JSON Response</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <span><pre class="highlight"><code><span class="p">{</span><span class="nt">"echo"</span><span class="p">:</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s2">"hello world"</span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// The same thing you'll get posted to your URL</span><span class="w"> </span></code></pre> </span>
