        <div class="docs-box" id="example-rejected-kyc-profile-callback"> 
         <h2>Example Rejected KYC callback</h2> 
         <div class="docs-box-body"> 
          <p> Here's a <strong>curl</strong> invokation that mimics a Bitex callback when a Kyc profile is rejected. You can copy and paste it directly into your terminal. </p> 
          <p> You can check the 'data.attributes.accepted_usage_tier' field in in the callback body to know if a user was accepted or rejected. It's null when it was rejected, and a string describing the usage tier when it's accepted. </p> 
          <p> Notice a KycProfile may change from accepted to rejected at any time, it may be accepted when first created then get rejected by further compliance procedures. </p> 
          <p> There's an API endpoint to lookup <a href="#list-all-rejection-reasons">all possible rejection reasons.</a> </p> 
          <strong>CURL Callback STUB</strong> 
          <div class="well well-sm"> 
           <textarea class="pastebox" rows="200">curl -X POST http://your_url.com/handler \
  -H "Webhook-Auth: your_api_key_sha_256" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" -d '{
    "data":{
      "id":"1",
      "type":"kyc_profiles",
      "attributes":{
        "user_id":3,
        "accepted_usage_tier":null,
        "usage_tier":"micro",
        "changed_by_customer_at": "2017-01-02T00:00:00.000Z",
        "reviewed_by_admin_at":"2017-01-02T00:00:00.000Z",
        "rejection_message":"Por favor completá tu DNI con una imágen mas legible",
        "first_name":"Juan",
        "last_name":"Perez",
        "personal_id_type":"dni",
        "personal_id_number":"30300300",
        "personal_id_issuer_country":"ar",
        "tax_id":null,
        "contact_email":null,
        "birth_date":null,
        "gender":null,
        "occupation":null,
        "home_address":null,
        "work_address":null,
        "phone_numbers":null,
        "politically_exposed_person":false,
        "nationality":null,
        "legal_entity":null,
        "company_name":null,
        "company_registration_number":null,
        "company_country":null,
        "company_address":null,
        "company_tax_id":null,
        "company_activity":null,
        "company_registration_date":null,
        "company_manager":null
      },
      "relationships":{
        "kyc_rejection_reason":{
          "data":{
            "id":"1",
            "type":"kyc_rejection_reasons"
          }
        }
      },
    },
    "included":[
      { "id":"1",
        "type":"kyc_rejection_reasons",
        "attributes":{
          "detail_es":"Algunos campos fueron inválidos",
          "detail_en":"Some fields were invalid",
          "detail_pt":"Alguns campos foram inválidos",
          "code":"invalid_fields"
        }
      }
    ]
  }'
</textarea> 
          </div> 
         </div>

        <hr> 
        <h1 id="api-class-reference">API Class Reference</h1> 
        <p> Some of our API methods return heterogeneous lists of objects, each object belongs to a given Class. Each Class has its own set of fields and possible field values. A USD Deposit, a Bid or a Sell Transaction are all examples of Classes used in our API. <br> In order to optimize data transfers we serialize Instances of these Classes as lists of numbers and text, but to help you deserializing them we came up with the following conventions: </p>
        <ul> 
         <li> The first value on the list represents the Class 
          <ol> 
           <li>Bid</li> 
           <li>Ask</li> 
           <li>Buy Transaction (created when one of your Bids is executed)</li> 
           <li>Sell Transaction (created when one of your Asks is executed)</li> 
           <li>Specie Deposit</li> 
           <li>Specie Withdrawal</li> 
           <li>USD Deposit</li> 
           <li>USD Withdrawal</li> 
          </ol> </li> 
         <li> The second value on the list represents the Instance id </li> 
         <li> The third value is the creation time as a UNIX timestamp </li> 
         <li> All the remaining values may vary depending on which Class it is. </li> 
        </ul> 
        <p></p> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <br> 
      <br> 
      <br>
